###begin title 16
Results
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 83 85 83 85 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 151 160 151 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 261 263 261 263 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 446 447 446 447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</sup>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Q</sub>
###xml 441 454 441 454 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NQQQY<sup>N</sup>/<sub>Q</sub>QQGQN</bold>
###xml 502 503 502 503 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sup>
###xml 504 505 504 505 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sub>
###xml 498 512 498 512 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GQQQ<sup>A</sup>/<sub>S</sub>NEYGRPQ</bold>
###xml 578 579 578 579 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Q</sup>
###xml 576 581 576 581 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NS<sup>Q</sup>/-</bold>
###xml 581 585 581 585 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">QGYN</bold>
###xml 585 586 585 586 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 587 588 587 588 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</sub>
###xml 585 588 585 588 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>&#8722;</sup>/<sub>N</sub></bold>
###xml 588 589 588 589 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sup>
###xml 590 591 590 591 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Q</sub>
###xml 593 594 593 594 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</sup>
###xml 595 596 595 596 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</sub>
###xml 588 598 588 598 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>S</sup>/<sub>Q</sub>YQ<sup>N</sup>/<sub>G</sub>GN</bold>
###xml 665 669 665 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Rost1">[67]</xref>
###xml 686 688 686 688 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LA</underline>
###xml 688 689 688 689 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sup>
###xml 690 691 690 691 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>
###xml 686 691 686 691 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><underline>LA</underline><sup>S</sup>/<sub>A</sub></bold>
###xml 691 692 691 692 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L</sup>
###xml 693 694 693 694 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</sub>
###xml 694 695 694 695 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 691 695 691 695 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>L</sup>/<sub>M</sub><underline>A</underline></bold>
###xml 761 762 761 762 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</sup>
###xml 763 764 763 764 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</sub>
###xml 765 767 765 767 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LA</underline>
###xml 768 769 768 769 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L</sup>
###xml 770 771 770 771 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</sub>
###xml 759 771 759 771 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SF<sup>G</sup>/<sub>T</sub>A<underline>LA</underline>S<sup>L</sup>/<sub>M</sub></bold>
###xml 771 772 771 772 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 771 776 771 776 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><underline>A</underline>SSFM</bold>
###xml 794 795 794 795 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sup>
###xml 796 797 796 797 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>
###xml 797 799 797 799 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LA</underline>
###xml 801 802 801 802 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 802 803 802 803 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Q</sup>
###xml 804 805 804 805 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sub>
###xml 792 809 792 809 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FS<sup>S</sup>/<sub>A</sub><underline>LA</underline>SM<underline>A</underline><sup>Q</sup>/<sub>S</sub>SYLG</bold>
###xml 886 888 886 888 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LA</underline>
###xml 890 891 890 891 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</underline>
###xml 886 891 886 891 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><underline>LA</underline>LL<underline>A</underline></bold>
###xml 977 981 977 981 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Douglas1">[68]</xref>
###xml 1001 1010 1001 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
The C-terminal part of Rnq1 encompasses a stretch of ten QG two-residue repeats, QG10, and four QN-rich regions interspersed by hydrophobic sequences (Figure 1A). In this work, we refer to QN-rich regions as QN1 through QN4, and hydrophobic patches preceding QG10, QN1, QN2, QN3 and QN4 are labeled A, B, C, D and E, respectively. QN1 is short and simple, whereas other QNs each contain two imperfect repeats: a tandem 11 aa repeat in QN3 - NQQQYN/QQQGQN, a 12 aa repeat separated by 2 aa in QN4 - GQQQA/SNEYGRPQ, and a more degenerate 14 aa repeat separated by 1 aa in QN2 - NSQ/-QGYN-/NS/QYQN/GGN. Hydrophobic patches, for which helical structure is predicted (; [67]), have a common LAS/AL/MA core sequence. More pair-wise similarity is seen for B and C - SFG/TALASL/MASSFM, and D and E - FSS/ALASMAQ/SSYLG. Interestingly, a similar hydrophobic patch in the N-terminal part of Rnq1 (LALLA, aa 94-98), has recently been implicated in the interaction with the Sis1 chaperone ([68]; indicated as O in Figure 1A).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 103 104 103 104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 100 104 100 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 228 237 228 237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 395 397 395 397 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 691 695 691 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 717 721 717 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 811 814 811 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CEN</italic>
###xml 618 623 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
To assess the role of individual sequence determinants of Rnq1 in maintaining and transmitting the [PIN+] prion, we designed a series of deletions lacking various combinations of Q-rich regions and adjacent hydrophobic patches (Figure 1A). For all these constructs: (i) the non-QN-rich N-terminal domain preceding the A patch (aa 1-132) is retained; (ii) deletions start/end at the borders of QG10 or QN-rich regions; (iii) internal deletions are "seamless", i.e. no additional amino acids are inserted at the junctions; (iv) no tags are attached at the termini to avoid possible interference of tag sequences; (v) in yeast, the expression of deletion constructs is controlled by the native RNQ1 promoter, the native RNQ1 terminator sequence follows the ORFs, and the constructs are introduced on a single-copy CEN vector.
###end p 18
###begin title 19
###xml 40 43 40 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 43 44 43 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
No one QN-rich region is essential for [PIN+] maintenance
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 80 81 80 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 185 194 185 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 225 226 225 226 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 228 232 228 232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 234 244 234 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 283 287 279 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 306 310 302 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 339 343 335 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 432 436 428 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 475 476 471 472 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 472 476 468 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 577 587 573 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s001">Figure S1A</xref>
###xml 843 844 839 840 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 840 844 836 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 873 874 869 870 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 870 874 866 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 893 897 889 893 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Derkatch4">[53]</xref>
###xml 898 902 894 898 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Liebman1">[69]</xref>
###xml 912 913 908 909 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 909 913 905 909 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 934 955 930 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
We first asked if any of the QN regions is essential for the maintenance of [PIN+]. Deletion constructs lacking one of the four QN regions, as well as an adjacent hydrophobic sequence (Figure 1A), were transformed into a [PIN+][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 strain expressing full-length RNQ1 controlled by the RNQ1 promoter. The plasmid-borne RNQ1 maintainer kept steady-state Rnq1 levels comparable to those in strains with endogenous RNQ1 and ensured stable maintenance of [PIN+] (not shown); steady state levels of deletion constructs were similar to those of full length Rnq1 (Figure S1A). Following transient co-expression of deletion constructs with full-length Rnq1 (to allow for transfer of the prion state), the maintainer plasmid was shuffled out, and the presence of prions composed of Rnq1 fragments, hereafter referred to as mini-[PIN+]s, was scored using the [PSI+] induction assay ([53],[69]; see [PSI+] Induction Assay in Materials and Methods).
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 43 44 43 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 54 61 54 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de novo</italic>
###xml 79 80 79 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 76 80 76 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 123 124 123 124 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 120 124 120 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 212 224 212 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SUP35NM::YFP</italic>
###xml 275 279 275 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL1</italic>
###xml 298 305 298 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ade1-14</italic>
###xml 352 356 352 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADE1</italic>
###xml 398 399 398 399 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 395 399 395 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 530 531 530 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 527 531 527 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 605 606 605 606 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 602 606 602 606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 673 677 673 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Patino1">[70]</xref>
###xml 678 682 678 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Zhou1">[71]</xref>
The assay relies on the requirement of [PIN+] for the de novo formation of [PSI+] and requires that the strain carry a [PSI+]-inducing construct and a reporter for the detection of [PSI+]. Our strain carried the SUP35NM::YFP inducer, under the control of a tightly regulated GAL1 promoter, and the ade1-14 reporter, a premature stop in the chromosomal ADE1 gene allowing to score the appearing [PSI+] colonies by their ability to grow on media lacking adenine. The Sup35NM::Yfp fusion was used as an auxiliary reporter during [PSI+] induction on galactose medium: its incorporation into newly forming [PSI+] aggregates allowed their visualization by fluorescent microscopy [70],[71].
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 9 0 9 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 146 147 146 147 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 205 206 197 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 244 245 236 237 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 241 245 233 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 416 417 408 409 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 413 417 405 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 429 430 421 422 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 523 524 515 516 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 520 524 512 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 565 572 557 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s2">Results</xref>
###xml 583 591 575 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 737 738 729 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 793 794 785 786 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 790 794 782 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 836 845 828 837 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1C</xref>
Figure 1B demonstrates that, after elimination of full-length Rnq1, cultures expressing deletion constructs lacking any one QN region remained Pin+ (similar data for Delta2D and Delta3E not shown). The Pin+ phenotype was determined by mini-[PIN+]s, as the propagation of the phenotype required the presence of Rnq1 fragments: the loss of deletion plasmids was always accompanied by the loss of ability to become [PSI+] (12-18 Leu- clones were analyzed for each construct; detailed analysis of mitotic stability of mini-[PIN+]s is presented later, in the section of Results including Figure 4). Also, Rnq1 fragments sustained the aggregated state: cells with bright fluorescent Rnq1::Cfp foci were detected in diploids from crosses of Pin+ cultures carrying Rnq1 deletion constructs with a [pin-] 64-D697 strain carrying pCUP-RNQ1::CFP (Figure 1C; hereafter this test is referred to as Rnq1::Cfp aggregation test).
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 403 405 403 405 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 438 440 438 440 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 472 473 472 473 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 469 473 469 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 589 593 589 593 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Vitrenko2">[65]</xref>
###xml 643 645 643 645 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 675 676 675 676 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 672 676 672 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 755 756 755 756 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 752 756 752 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 786 795 786 795 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 812 813 812 813 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 809 813 809 813 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
The fact that fragments lacking QN1, QN2, QN3 or QN4 exist in an aggregated self-perpetuating state in the cultures not expressing wild type Rnq1 showed that no one QN region in Rnq1 is essential for prion maintenance. This raised an intriguing possibility of the redundancy in the prion-forming ability of QN-rich determinants. The alternative possibility, that the retained in all constructs Q-rich QG10 and/or a sequence upstream of QG10 are capable of maintaining [PIN+] even in the absence of QN regions, appeared highly unlikely based on earlier studies of N-terminal Rnq1 fragments [65]. It was further excluded by demonstrating that QG10 is not required for mini-[PIN+] establishment, and that the QN-rich C-terminus is indispensable for mini-[PIN+]s in our experimental setup (Figure S2). Thus, the [PIN+] prion domain is located in the QN-rich C-terminus, but no one QN region in Rnq1 is essential for the maintenance of the prion state, suggesting that Rnq1 prion domain carries multiple determinants capable of independently supporting the prion state.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Multiple aggregation determinants in Rnq1
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 195 203 195 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 456 465 444 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
To determine which QN regions could drive prion-like aggregation of Rnq1, bacterially expressed Rnq1 fragments lacking three out of four QN regions were tested for the propensity to form amyloid in vitro. Incubation of proteins encompassing only QN2 (DeltaB1D3E4), QN3 (DeltaB1C2E4) or QN4 (DeltaB1C2D3) with Thioflavin T (ThT) resulted in a shift of the ThT excitation spectrum and increase of ThT fluorescence at 483 nm, indicative of amyloid formation (Figure 2A). Sigmoidal fluorescence kinetics was consistent with the presence of a rate-limiting nucleation step followed by a fiber growth phase. The QN1-bearing protein (DeltaC2D3E4) did not form amyloid even at very high concentrations.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 122 130 106 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
QN2 (DeltaB1C2E4), QN3 (DeltaB1C2E4), and QN4 (DeltaB1C2D3), but not QN1 (DeltaC2D3E4), can drive amyloid fiber formation in vitro.
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 18 26 18 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 697 707 673 683 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 782 791 750 759 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
(A-D) Kinetics of in vitro aggregation of recombinant proteins monitored by ThT fluorescence. (A) Unseeded reactions. Concentrations: QN1 - 100 microM, QN2 - 70 microM, QN3 - 80 microM, QN4 - 70 microM. Shown are averages and standard deviations of 2-hour time points based on 3-5 independent experiments. (B) Concentration dependence of the lag phase for QN4 aggregation. (C) Elimination of lag phase in seeded reactions for QN2 and QN4. Concentrations of soluble proteins were 70 microM. (D) Retention of lag phase in seeded reactions for QN3. Concentration of soluble protein was 80 microM. (E) Summary of the analysis of cross-seeding between Rnq1 fragments carrying different QN regions (see Figure S3A). QN1,2 and QN3,4 correspond, respectively, to DeltaD3E4 and DeltaB1C2 in Figure 1A. (+) indicates disappearance or, in the case of QN3, reduction of the lag phase; (-) indicates no change in the kinetics of fiber formation upon the addition of seeds to soluble proteins. (F-P) Transmission electron micrographs of negatively stained fibers. In (N-P) fibers were treated with papain. Arrows show lateral association of fibers (L), ring-like oligomers (J, L inset, M, N insets) and twisted appearance of QN2 fibers (F,N).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 327 336 307 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 453 462 433 442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 708 717 688 697 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 722 732 702 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 874 883 838 847 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 1140 1149 1104 1113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 1228 1234 1192 1198 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90-231</sub>
###xml 1244 1248 1208 1212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Baskakov1">[72]</xref>
###xml 1382 1391 1346 1355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 1396 1406 1360 1370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 1517 1522 1481 1486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ibid.</italic>
Aggregation kinetics of QN2 and QN4 was similar except that at equal protein concentrations the lag phase was slightly shorter for QN4. The threshold protein concentration for fiber formation was approximately15-20 microM, and the length of the lag phase was reproducible and concentration-dependent in the 30-80 microM range (Figure 2B and not shown). When reactions were seeded by preformed homologous fibers, the lag phase was completely eliminated (Figure 2C). In the cross-seeding reactions QN2 and QN4 could efficiently seed and be seeded by larger Rnq1 fragments, as long as they encompassed, respectively, QN2 and QN4 regions, implicating these regions in specific interactions during cross-seeding (Figure 2E and Figure S3A). For QN3, the threshold concentration was higher, approximately80microM, and the lag phase was considerably longer compared to QN2 and QN4 (Figure 2A), indicating that QN3 has a weaker aggregation propensity. The kinetics of seeded QN3 reactions was also distinct from QN2 and QN4: the QN3 fluorescence curve remained sigmoidal and a 10-20 hr lag phase was observed regardless of the amount of seed added (Figure 2D and data not shown). Such unusual kinetics was previously observed for the PrP90-231 fragment [72]. Also, QN3 was only capable of self-seeding, but could not template or be templated by a fragment including both QN3 and QN4 (QN3,4; Figure 2E and Figure S3A). QN3,4 aggregation could only be self-seeded or seeded by QN4 and there was no lag phase in these reactions (ibid.). This suggests that the conformation of the QN3 region in the fibers made from a Rnq1 fragment in which QN3 is the only aggregation determinant is different from conformations QN3 can take when combined with other QN regions.
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 93 115 89 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2F&#8211;2H and 2J&#8211;2L</xref>
###xml 471 475 455 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Lashuel1">[73]</xref>
###xml 476 480 460 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Shorter1">[74]</xref>
###xml 570 586 554 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2J and 2L</xref>
###xml 680 696 664 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2I and 2M</xref>
Electron microscopy revealed networks of >1 microm-long fibers in QN2, QN3, and QN4 samples (Figure 2F-2H and 2J-2L). Fibers were approximately18-25 nm in diameter and unbranched, but frequently 2 or more fibers were associated laterally for part of their length producing thicker rope-like structures. In addition to fibers, we observed ring-like structures strikingly similar to oligomeric species previously seen during fiber formation by other amyloidogenic proteins [73],[74]; the oligomers were either lying separately or distributed irregularly along the fibers (Figure 2J and 2L inset). Similar fibers and oligomers were formed in the same conditions by full-length Rnq1 (Figure 2I and 2M).
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 190 199 190 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2P</xref>
###xml 252 261 252 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2N</xref>
###xml 344 353 344 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2N</xref>
###xml 546 555 546 555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2O</xref>
As expected of amyloid, QN2 and QN4 fibers were protease-resistant. After hydrolysis with papain, they remained long, but became thinner (<10 nm in diameter). QN4 fibers became very smooth (Figure 2P), and QN2 fibers retained their twisted appearance (Figure 2N). Ring-like oligomers also remained and their structure became even more obvious (Figure 2N insets). Unexpectedly, papain treatment eliminated all long QN3 fibers, although occasional clusters of atypical aggregates with few protruding thread-like structures could still be detected (Figure 2O).
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 125 133 125 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
Thus, the Rnq1 prion domain encompasses three distinct QN-rich determinants that can independently drive aggregation of Rnq1 in vitro: QN2, QN3 and QN4. Among them, QN3 is weaker, and QN3 aggregates are somewhat atypical.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 369 379 369 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3SB</xref>
Lack of aggregation of QN1 suggests that its 12 aa long QN-rich stretch is not sufficient to drive aggregation of Rnq1 independently and confirms the lack of strong aggregation determinants upstream of QN1. However, using ThT fluorescence analysis and TEM, we demonstrated that the 12 aa peptide corresponding to QN1 region alone readily formed typical amyloid fibers (Figure 3SB and data not shown), suggesting that this region may function as aggregation determinant in the presence of other QN regions.
###end p 32
###begin title 33
Transmission of the prion state to Rnq1 fragments with one or two QN regions.
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 50 51 50 51 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 47 51 47 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 104 108 104 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 146 155 146 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 319 320 313 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 316 320 310 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 368 369 362 363 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 365 369 359 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 553 571 547 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s001">Figure S1B and S1C</xref>
(A.B) The prion state can be transmitted from [PIN+] to Rnq1 fragments encompassing either QN2 or QN4. [PSI+] induction assay was performed as in Figure 1B. Shown is growth on SD-Ade after incubation at 20degreesC for 11 (A) and 13 (B) days. (C) Rnq1 fragments carrying only QN1 or/and QN3 do not co-aggregate with [PIN+]. Sedimentation analysis of the lysates of [PIN+] cells expressing both full-length Rnq1 and indicated deletion constructs; the WT Rnq1 and the QN1,QN3 panels show same lanes in the top and the bottom parts of the Western blot. See Figure S1B and S1C for steady state levels of Rnq1 fragments used in these experiments.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
The prion state can be transmitted to Rnq1 fragments carrying either QN2 or QN4
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 52 59 52 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 61 65 61 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 187 191 187 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 203 204 203 204 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 209 210 209 210 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 206 210 206 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 212 222 212 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 260 261 256 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 257 261 253 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 350 351 346 347 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 347 351 343 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 391 400 387 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 434 435 426 427 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 533 534 517 518 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 530 534 514 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 620 629 604 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 645 646 629 630 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 745 746 729 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 742 746 726 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
To test which QN regions could maintain prion state in vivo, RNQ1 fragments encoding any one QN region or all possible combinations of two QN regions were substituted for the full-length RNQ1 in the [PIN+][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 strain. As seen from the [PSI+] induction test, all fragments carrying two QN regions could be converted into mini-[PIN+]s as long as QN2 or QN4 were retained (Figure 3A; DeltaB1D3 cultures were also Pin+ and in this test were similar to DeltaB1C2 and DeltaB1E4, not shown). Furthermore, low-level [PSI+] induction was detected even when using the constructs encompassing only QN2 or QN4 (Figure 3B). This weak Pin+ phenotype was confirmed using the Sup35NM::Yfp reporter: cells with bright foci indicative of [PSI+] appearance were readily detected in cultures expressing either QN2 or QN4, but not in the empty vector control (not shown).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 112 113 112 113 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 130 134 130 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 153 169 153 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3A and 3B</xref>
###xml 270 271 270 271 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 267 271 267 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 401 402 401 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 398 402 398 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 445 446 445 446 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 442 446 442 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 476 480 476 480 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 482 491 482 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 537 538 537 538 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 534 538 534 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
On the contrary, cultures expressing Rnq1 fragments encompassing only QN1 and QN3, alone or together, became Pin- after wild type RNQ1 was shuffled out (Figure 3A and 3B; also no aggregate-containing cells were detected when Sup35NM::Yfp was used to screen for rare [PSI+]s). We also found no evidence that QN1 and QN3-bearing fragments were taking on a prion state that was incapable of inducing [PSI+]: these fragments remained soluble in [PIN+] cells before elimination of RNQ1 (Figure 3C), and after the shuffle the lack of mini-[PIN+] aggregates was confirmed by a diffuse distribution of the reporter in the Rnq1::Cfp aggregation test (not shown).
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 70 71 70 71 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 67 71 67 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 95 103 95 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 282 290 282 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 292 301 292 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 345 346 345 346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 342 346 342 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 422 423 422 423 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 419 423 419 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 613 614 613 614 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 610 614 610 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 701 702 701 702 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 705 712 705 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de novo</italic>
###xml 714 718 714 718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 770 774 770 774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 782 783 782 783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 779 783 779 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 788 789 788 789 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 785 789 785 789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 791 801 791 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 832 833 828 829 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 848 855 844 851 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s013">Text S1</xref>
###xml 877 878 873 874 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 981 997 977 993 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3A and 3B</xref>
###xml 1266 1274 1262 1270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1284 1291 1280 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Ability of Rnq1 fragments carrying either QN2 or QN4 to form mini-[PIN+]s is in agreement with in vitro data and further indicates that these regions represent independent prion determinants. Also, considering the specificity of cross-seeding of QN2- and QN4-encompassing fragments in vitro (Figure 2E), transmission of the prion state from [PIN+] to fragments carrying either QN2 or QN4 suggest that in the wild type [PIN+] prion both QN2 and QN4 regions are involved in prion formation and are available for templating. (To prove that the prion state was transmitted to Rnq1 fragments from the pre-existing [PIN+], and that Rnq1 fragments expressed from single-copy plasmids did not induce mini-[PIN+]s de novo, RNQ1 deletion constructs were substituted for wild type RNQ1 in [pin-][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694, which resulted in Pin- cultures; see Text S1). The more robust Pin+ phenotype observed when QN2 or QN4 were combined with either QN1 or QN3 compared to QN2 or QN4 alone (Figure 3A and 3B) suggests that QN1 and QN3 are also involved in prion formation. However, we found no indication that the prion state could be transmitted to fragments carrying only these QN regions. One possibility, consistent with the weak amyloid-forming propensity of QN1 and QN3 in vitro, is that in vivo their aggregation is contingent on the presence of QN2 or QN4.
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 56 59 56 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 59 60 59 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 71 74 71 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 74 75 74 75 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
A barrier for the transmission of the prion state from [PIN+] to mini-[PIN+]s
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 13 29 13 29 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3A and 3B</xref>
###xml 38 39 38 39 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 88 89 88 89 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 85 89 85 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 140 141 140 141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 137 141 137 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 197 198 197 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 194 198 194 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 336 337 336 337 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 333 337 333 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 340 349 340 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 364 365 364 365 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 361 365 361 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 417 418 417 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 497 500 497 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 500 501 500 501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 556 557 556 557 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 553 557 553 557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 696 697 696 697 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 693 697 693 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 708 711 708 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 711 712 711 712 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
As seen from Figure 3A and 3B, the Pin+ phenotype of cultures carrying shorter mini-[PIN+]s is notably reduced compared to the original [PIN+] strain. Furthermore, quantifying the frequency of [PSI+] induction using the Sup35NM::Yfp reporter revealed that deletion of any QN region except QN1 resulted in a drop in the induction of [PSI+] (Figure S4). Reduced [PSI+] induction could reflect (i) the appearance of [pin-] cells due to inefficient transmission of the prion state from the wild type [PIN+], i.e. transmission barrier; (ii) accumulation of [pin-] cells because Rnq1 fragments were deficient in maintaining the prion state in the absence of full-length Rnq1; (iii) poor seeding of [PSI+] by mini-[PIN+]s.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 64 65 64 65 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 133 136 133 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 220 224 220 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 299 302 299 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 311 312 311 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 308 312 308 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 335 344 335 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 390 391 390 391 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 387 391 387 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 447 448 447 448 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 444 448 444 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 462 463 462 463 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 459 463 459 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 477 478 477 478 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 559 560 559 560 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 568 569 568 569 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 580 589 580 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 659 663 659 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 708 709 708 709 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 758 759 758 759 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 755 759 755 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 891 900 891 900 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4E</xref>
###xml 934 935 934 935 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 931 935 931 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1098 1107 1098 1107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 1165 1166 1165 1166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1162 1166 1162 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1221 1222 1221 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1218 1222 1218 1222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1272 1281 1272 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 1286 1295 1286 1295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 1516 1517 1512 1513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1513 1517 1509 1513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1526 1535 1522 1531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4D</xref>
###xml 1537 1546 1533 1542 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s007">Figure S7</xref>
To eliminate the last possibility as the only cause for weak Pin+ phenotypes in cultures expressing Rnq1 fragments, we analyzed the [PIN] status of individual cells in these cultures. After shuffling out the full-length RNQ1, the cultures were colony purified, and individual colonies were screened via the [PSI+] induction assay (see Figure S5 for a scheme of experiments). If reduced [PSI+] formation were exclusively due to poor seeding of [PSI+] by mini-[PIN+]s, a weak Pin+ phenotype was expected for all colonies. However, most cultures yielded both Pin+ and Pin- colonies (Figure 4A) indicating that substitution of deletion constructs for full-length RNQ1 lead to the loss of prion in some cells. Pin- colonies were mitotically stable, and their [pin-] status was confirmed by the Rnq1::Cfp aggregation test (not shown) and, for several colonies, by sedimentation analysis (see e.g. Figure 4E). Although the proportion of [pin-] cells varied widely in cultures expressing the same Rnq1 fragment, there was a clear dependence of distributions upon the number and identity of QN regions (see Figure S6 for distributions). In most cases, the proportion of [pin-] cells correlated with the degree of reduction of [PSI+] induction prior to colony purification (compare Figure 4A and Figure S4). In agreement with genetic data, soluble Rnq1 was detected in the lysates of the cultures expressing all Rnq1 deletion constructs except DeltaB1, and the proportion of soluble Rnq1 correlated with the percentage of [pin-] cells (Figure 4D, Figure S7, and data not shown).
###end p 41
###begin title 42
###xml 72 73 72 73 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 90 94 90 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Transmission barrier for the conversion of Rnq1 fragments into mini-[PIN+]s by wild-type [PIN+].
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 20 24 20 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
