###xml 416 420 416 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 423 426 423 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 435 436 435 436 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 508 509 508 509 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 505 509 505 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 728 729 728 729 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 725 729 725 729 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 772 773 772 773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 769 773 769 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 838 839 838 839 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 835 839 835 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1046 1047 1046 1047 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1043 1047 1043 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1236 1237 1232 1233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1233 1237 1229 1233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1549 1558 1529 1538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1673 1674 1645 1646 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1670 1674 1642 1646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1705 1706 1673 1674 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1702 1706 1670 1674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1718 1719 1686 1687 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1715 1719 1683 1687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1803 1812 1767 1776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 1840 1841 1804 1805 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1837 1841 1801 1805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1864 1873 1828 1837 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
(A) Substitution of RNQ1 deletion constructs for full-length RNQ1 in a [PIN+] strain leads to the appearance of [pin-] cells. Plasmid shuffle was performed as in Figure 1B. After selecting for the loss of full-length RNQ1 on FOA, cultures now expressing only Rnq1 fragments were transferred to SD-Leu,His and then colony purified on this medium. 40 colonies from each culture were screened for the presence of mini-[PIN+]s via the [PSI+] induction test. Each data point represents the percentage of mini-[PIN+] colonies in one independent culture. The total number of cultures analyzed for each deletion is shown below the graph. Bars indicate average for all independent cultures. (B) Analysis of mitotic stability of mini-[PIN+]s reveals the presence of stable mini-[PIN+]s for all single and double deletions. Randomly chosen mini-[PIN+] isolates from the experiment described in 4A were passed once on SD-Leu,His and then colony purified again. Colonies from this second round of subcloning were analyzed as described in 4A. Several mini-[PIN+] isolates with high mitotic stability were also obtained for Delta1C2D3 in a separate experiment (MK and ID unpublished observations). (C-E) Sedimentation analyses of cell lysates. In [PIN+] cells still co-expressing wild-type Rnq1 (C) and after elimination of wild-type Rnq1 (D), DeltaC2, DeltaD3 and DeltaE4 are detected in both soluble and aggregated fractions, whereas DeltaB1 is aggregated. In (C) paired panels are from the same lanes at the top and the bottom of the Western blot. For (D), see Figure S7 for finer analysis of Delta2D and DeltaE4 aggregation. (E) Rnq1 fragments are fully aggregated in stable mini-[PIN+] isolates. A DeltaD3 mini-[PIN+] and a [pin-] colony were isolated from a DeltaD3-expressing culture in experiment described in Figure 4A; stability of the mini-[PIN+] was determined as in Figure 4B.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 85 86 85 86 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 82 86 82 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 182 183 182 183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 179 183 179 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 271 272 271 272 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 268 272 268 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 286 287 286 287 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 298 299 298 299 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 420 421 420 421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 417 421 417 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 480 481 480 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 477 481 477 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 602 603 602 603 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 605 614 605 614 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 625 634 625 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 681 682 681 682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 678 682 678 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 746 747 746 747 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 743 747 743 747 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 899 900 899 900 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 896 900 896 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 944 953 944 953 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 978 979 978 979 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 975 979 975 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1192 1201 1192 1201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4E</xref>
###xml 1370 1371 1370 1371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1367 1371 1367 1371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1407 1408 1407 1408 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1404 1408 1404 1408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1516 1517 1516 1517 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1513 1517 1513 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1694 1710 1694 1710 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A and 4B</xref>
###xml 1715 1724 1715 1724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 1824 1828 1824 1828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 1888 1889 1888 1889 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1885 1889 1885 1889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
We next asked if Rnq1 fragments were unable to form efficiently propagating mini-[PIN+]s, and if this deficiency in prion propagation could alone account for the accumulation of [pin-] cells, or there indeed was a barrier for the transmission of the prion state from [PIN+] to mini-[PIN+]s. The Pin+ colonies obtained by the colony purification described in the previous paragraph represent single-cell derived mini-[PIN+] isolates. To analyze mitotic stability of these mini-[PIN+]s, we passed them once on SD-Leu,His, then colony purified again and determined what proportion of colonies remained Pin+ (Figure 4B; see also Figure S5 for a scheme of experiments). Even though [pin-] cells did accumulate in a considerable proportion of mini-[PIN+] isolates, the data clearly indicate the existence of transmission barriers. Specifically, for all single and double QN deletions, there were mini-[PIN+]s that transmitted to all mitotic progeny (Figure 4B). Several such mini-[PIN+]s were selected for each construct and their high stability was confirmed by more extensive analysis (not shown). Furthermore, in these stable isolates, Rnq1 fragments were detected only in aggregated fractions (Figure 4E). This demonstrates that respective Rnq1 fragments are fully competent in maintaining the prion state. Also, for all deletion constructs, the average proportion of [PIN+] cells was much higher in mini-[PIN+] isolates than in original post-shuffle cultures, even though the number of cell divisions from a mini-[PIN+] cell to the second round of colony purification was no less than the number of divisions from the loss of full-length Rnq1 to the first round of colony purifications (compare Figure 4A and 4B and Figure S6). This indicates that the prion state was lost more frequently upon the elimination of full-length RNQ1 or soon after. Our finding of stable and unstable mini-[PIN+] isolates may reflect the process prion strain formation, which is another hallmark of transmission barriers.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 77 78 77 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 114 118 114 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 256 257 256 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 253 257 253 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 521 530 505 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4C</xref>
###xml 694 695 674 675 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 691 695 671 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
In a different approach we analyzed the aggregation of Rnq1 fragments in [PIN+] cells prior to the elimination of RNQ1. The rationale was that in the case of a transmission barrier Rnq1 fragments should remain partially soluble even in the presence of [PIN+]. Indeed, even DeltaC2, DeltaD3 and DeltaE4 single deletions, for which fairly weak transmission barriers were indicated by genetic analysis, were detected in soluble fractions, and only DeltaB1, for which the weakest barrier was seen, appeared fully aggregated (Figure 4C and not shown). For double and triple deletions, only DeltaB1C2 was mostly aggregated, whereas other Rnq1 fragments remained mostly soluble in the presence of [PIN+], consistent with strength of respective transmission barriers (not shown).
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 95 96 95 96 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 92 96 92 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 110 111 110 111 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 107 111 107 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 282 291 278 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
Thus, we demonstrated that there is a barrier for the transmission of the prion state from [PIN+] to mini-[PIN+]s. None of the QN regions can ensure a barrier-free transmission, and elimination of any QN region results in the transmission barrier (a barrier towards DeltaB1 seen in Figure 4A is very weak but was confirmed in other experiments; MK and ID unpublished observations).
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 65 67 65 67 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
Contribution of oligopeptide repeats, hydrophobic patches, and QG10 to the transmission barrier
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 154 163 154 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 490 499 490 499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 504 513 504 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s008">Figure S8</xref>
###xml 535 538 531 534 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1/2</sub>
###xml 637 640 625 628 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2/3</sub>
###xml 1114 1115 1098 1099 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1111 1115 1095 1099 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1160 1163 1140 1143 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1/3</sub>
###xml 1521 1525 1501 1505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Vitrenko2">[65]</xref>
###xml 1569 1570 1549 1550 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1566 1570 1546 1550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1619 1620 1599 1600 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1616 1620 1596 1600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
The complexity of Rnq1 prion domain goes beyond the presence of four QN-rich regions. Three QN regions, QN2, QN3 and QN4, encompass oligopeptide repeats (Figure 1A). To probe the contribution of these repeats to the transmission of the prion state, we tested if removing a part of a repeat-containing QN region is equivalent to its complete deletion. Experiments described in this section were performed with a set of C-terminal truncations gradually removing parts of regions QN3 and QN4 (Figure 5A and Figure S8). Comparison of Delta1/2 3E4 (terminates right after the first oligopeptide of the QN3 repeat) with DeltaD3E4, and of Delta2/34 (the first oligopeptide of the QN4 repeat is preserved intact) with DeltaE4, shows that retaining only the first oligopeptide of the repeat is enough to lower the transmission barrier compared to complete deletion of the respective QN region, but is not equivalent to retaining the whole QN region. This suggests that each oligopeptide contributes to prion formation, and that retaining the repeated structure is not essential for this contribution. The appearance of [pin-] cells even in the cultures expressing Delta1/34 (retains the complete QN4 repeat but lacks the very C-terminal QN-rich stretch and the preceding non-QN-rich sequence) indicates that both the repeats and the unique part of QN4 contribute to the prion conformation. The gradual increase of the transmission barrier with progressing C-terminal truncations is consistent with observations of Vitrenko et al. [65] who noted an increase in the number of [pin-] cytoductants following the transmission of [PIN+] to a smaller set of Gfp-tagged C-terminally truncated Rnq1 fragments.
###end p 48
###begin title 49
###xml 84 86 84 86 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
Contribution of parts of regions QN3 and QN4 (A), hydrophobic patches (B, C), and QG10 (D) to the loss of prion state upon substitution of Rnq1 fragments for full-length Rnq1.
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 33 42 33 42 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 181 191 181 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s001">Figure S1D</xref>
###xml 238 247 238 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s008">Figure S8</xref>
###xml 252 261 252 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s009">Figure S9</xref>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 302 306 302 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Experiments were performed as in Figure 4A. Bars show average for 6 (A), 2 (B), 3 (C), and 3 (D) independent experiments; standard error of the mean (SEM) is shown for (A,C,D). See Figure S1D for steady state levels of Rnq1 fragments and Figure S8 and Figure S9 for map, data and the analysis of mini-[PIN+]s formed by these fragments.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 103 112 103 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 326 327 318 319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 456 465 440 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 590 591 574 575 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 587 591 571 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 734 743 694 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 748 766 708 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s009">Figure S9A and S9B</xref>
Another feature of Rnq1 prion domain is the alternating pattern of QN regions and hydrophobic patches (Figure 1A) with a QN-rich region at the C-terminus. Our analysis suggests the importance of the C-terminal location of the last QN region: compared to DeltaE4 and DeltaD3E4 ending with QN-rich regions, the proportion of Pin+ cells was sharply reduced in cultures expressing Delta4 and Delta3E4 fragments carrying hydrophobic patches at their C-termini (Figure 5B). The importance of alternating QN regions and hydrophobic patches is not as clear. For example, the proportion of mini-[PIN+] cells was lower in Delta2 cultures than in DeltaC2 and Delta2D, but there was no significant difference between Delta3, DeltaD3 and Delta3E (Figure 5C and Figure S9A and S9B).
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 11 13 11 13 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 81 99 81 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s002">Figure S2C and S2D</xref>
###xml 227 228 219 220 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 224 228 216 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 247 251 239 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 285 286 277 278 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 282 286 274 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 338 339 330 331 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 335 339 327 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 342 351 334 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5D</xref>
###xml 353 371 345 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s009">Figure S9C and S9D</xref>
###xml 410 412 402 404 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
Finally, QG10, which does not lead to a transmission barrier when deleted alone (Figure S2C and S2D), may contribute to barriers if deleted with other regions. Compared to DeltaB1C2, more of DeltaQGB1C2 remained soluble in [PIN+] cells, and after RNQ1 was eliminated and wild type [PIN+] was lost, a higher proportion of cells became [pin-] (Figure 5D, Figure S9C and S9D and data not shown). In this aspect QG10 is similar to QN1, for which effects on transmission barriers are seen mainly in the context of larger deletions.
###end p 52
###begin title 53
Cooperative action of QN-determinants in prion conformation
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 186 187 186 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 325 326 325 326 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 427 428 427 428 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 424 428 424 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 626 627 626 627 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 623 627 623 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 906 907 906 907 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 903 907 903 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1090 1091 1090 1091 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1087 1091 1087 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
As shown in the previous sections, prion domain of Rnq1 encompasses multiple QN-rich aggregation determinants. None of them is essential for the transmission of the prion state from [PIN+] to Rnq1 fragments, and analysis of transmission to Rnq1 fragments with different sets of QN regions indicates that in the wild type [PIN+] prion several QN regions are aggregated and can be used for templating. Yet, transmission from [PIN+] to essentially any Rnq1 fragment involves crossing a barrier, which is similar to the barriers observed during interspecies transmission of other prions. These barriers are hard to explain if [PIN+] just included several relatively autonomous aggregated regions. Indeed, single aa mismatches, always present in the case of interspecies transmissions, could interfere with the transmission at particular short regions, but there are no single amino acid mismatches between [PIN+] and Rnq1 fragments; rather, whole aggregation-prone domains are removed. We hypothesized that transmission barriers are determined by an overall prion conformation and that the [PIN+] prion conformation is a result of co-operative action of multiple determinants that can transmit the prion state independently of each other.
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 48 49 48 49 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 45 49 45 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 546 547 546 547 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 543 547 543 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 693 694 693 694 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 690 694 690 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Our model for conformational organzation of [PIN+] and the mechanism of transmission barriers stipulates that transmission of the prion state between Rnq1 and its fragments involves templating by the exactly matching QN regions. Yet, having a common QN region capable of propagating the prion state is not sufficient for barrier-free transmission because all regions, including those not participating in templating, contribute to the overall conformation and, consequently, to conformational barriers. The conformation of the resulting mini-[PIN+] is also a product of co-operative action of all determinants present in the Rnq1 fragment and, consequently, is different from the original [PIN+], even though there is not a single amino acid mismatch in the templating region.
###end p 55
###begin p 56
###xml 154 155 154 155 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 151 155 151 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 244 245 244 245 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 241 245 241 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 259 260 259 260 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 256 260 256 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 311 312 311 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 308 312 308 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 326 327 326 327 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 323 327 323 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 518 519 518 519 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 515 519 515 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 533 534 533 534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 530 534 530 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 613 614 613 614 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 610 614 610 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
The following predictions can be made based on this model: (i) there should be a reciprocal barrier for the transmission of the prion state from mini-[PIN+]s to the full-length Rnq1; transmission of prion state between Rnq1 fragments (mini-[PIN+] to mini-[PIN+]) should also occur across barriers (ii) mini-[PIN+] to mini-[PIN+] transmission should require the presence of a common QN region; (iii) one common prion determinant should generally allow for some level of transmission; (iv) relative strength of mini-[PIN+] to mini-[PIN+] barriers may be different compared to the transmission from the original [PIN+], even if the same QN regions are involved in templating.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 55 56 55 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 104 113 104 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 115 119 115 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 210 214 210 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 360 369 360 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
To test these predictions, we utilized stable mini-[PIN+] isolates obtained in experiments described in Figure 4B. LEU2-marked RNQ1 fragment constructs were substituted for the URA3-marked ones. Then wild type RNQ1 or various RNQ1 deletion constructs were introduced by transformation, and plasmid shuffle experiment was performed as previously described (see Figure 1B).
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 0 9 0 9 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 69 70 69 70 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 66 70 66 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 93 97 93 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 124 125 124 125 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 121 125 121 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 206 207 206 207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 203 207 203 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 345 346 345 346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 342 346 342 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Figure 6A shows the existence of transmission barriers from mini-[PIN+]s towards full-length RNQ1, confirming that mini-[PIN+]s indeed represent prion conformational variants distinct from the original [PIN+] supported by full length Rnq1. The strength of the reciprocal barrier correlated with the strength of the transmission barrier from [PIN+] towards the respective Rnq1 fragment for most constructs (e.g. Delta2D and DeltaB1E4), but there were several notable exceptions to this rule (e.g. Delta3E).
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 109 110 109 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 106 110 106 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 138 147 138 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 216 217 212 213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 213 217 209 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 285 293 277 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 453 462 437 446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 532 533 512 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 529 533 509 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Importance of the presence of a common QN region was confirmed by transmitting the prion state from mini-[PIN+]s to other Rnq1 fragments. Figure 6B illustrates the lack of transmission between the DeltaB1C2 mini-[PIN+] and the DeltaD3E4 fragment. This result is in full agreement with in vitro data: DeltaB1C2 (QN3,4) and DeltaD3E4 (QN1,2) were unable to cross-seed each other while efficiently seeding QN4- and QN2-containing constructs, respectively (Figure 2E). Similarly, transmission was impossible from the DeltaB1E4 mini-[PIN+] to Delta2D3E (not shown).
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 77 78 77 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 415 424 415 424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 435 444 435 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 511 512 507 508 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 508 512 504 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 613 622 597 606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 638 647 622 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
###xml 777 778 757 758 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 774 778 754 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 794 803 770 779 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 881 890 849 858 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 970 971 934 935 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 967 971 931 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 985 994 945 954 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
After establishing the specificity of QN-based templating, pairs of mini-[PIN+]s and Rnq1 fragments encompassing only one common QN region were used to demonstrate that each of the four QN regions could independently transmit the prion state. For QN2 and QN4, multiple examples of this ability were obtained, since the prion state could be transmitted to Rnq1 fragments encompassing only QN2 and QN4, respectively (Figure 7A; see also Figure 3B). Other examples include the transmission from DeltaB1E4 mini-[PIN+] to DeltaD3 for QN2-driven transmission, and from DeltaB1C2 to DeltaD3 for QN4-driven transmission (Figure 7A; data shown in Figure 7D). The ability of QN1 to template matching sequences in Rnq1-based prions was deduced from the transmission from Delta2D mini-[PIN+] to DeltaD3E4 (Figure 7A; data shown in 7E), despite no transmission from DeltaB1C2 to DeltaD3E4 (see Figure 6B). Finally, templating by QN3 was shown by transmission from DeltaB1E4 mini-[PIN+] to Delta2D (Figure 7A; data shown in 7C), despite no transmission from DeltaB1E4 to Delta2D3E.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 116 117 116 117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 113 117 113 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 135 136 135 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 132 136 132 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 139 151 139 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7B&#8211;7E</xref>
###xml 361 362 361 362 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 358 362 358 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 386 387 386 387 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 383 387 383 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 454 463 442 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 501 502 485 486 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 498 502 482 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 556 565 536 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 673 674 649 650 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 670 674 646 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 714 715 690 691 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 711 715 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 788 797 760 769 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 868 884 832 848 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7B and 7E</xref>
###xml 1165 1166 1129 1130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1162 1166 1126 1130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1280 1281 1244 1245 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1277 1281 1241 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1360 1361 1308 1309 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1357 1361 1305 1309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1447 1456 1387 1396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
The strength of transmission barriers can be strikingly different when the same Rnq1 fragment is seeded by mini-[PIN+]s instead of [PIN+] (Figure 7B-7E). Changes in transmission barriers emphasize the leading role of QN2 and QN4 regions in Rnq1-based prions as removal of one of these regions increases the importance of the other. For example, compared to [PIN+], QN2-lacking mini-[PIN+]s Delta2D and DeltaB1C2 are less efficient in converting DeltaE4 (Figure 7B), and QN4-lacking DeltaB1E4 mini-[PIN+] has a dramatically reduced transmission to DeltaC2 (Figure 7C). The contribution of QN3 to the transmission barrier is also further underscored. When a Delta3E mini-[PIN+] is used for templating instead of [PIN+], the transmission barrier is simultaneously increased towards Delta2D (Figure 7C) and reduced towards the QN4-lacking DeltaE4 and DeltaD3E4 fragments (Figure 7B and 7E). It appears that QN3 modulates the contribution of QN2 and QN4 to the prion conformation and/or transmission, and elimination of QN3 increases the involvement of QN2 and decreases the involvement of QN4. The more complex contribution of the QN3 region to the conformation of [PIN+] is exemplified by the transmission to two similar constructs differing only in hydrophobic patch B: whereas [PIN+] or DeltaB1C2 could template Delta1C2D3 but not DeltaB1C2D3, Delta3E mini-[PIN+] transmitted prion state to both Delta1C2D3 and DeltaB1C2D3 with similar efficiency (Figure 7A and data not shown).
###end p 61
###begin title 62
Cooperative action of QN regions determines transmission barriers for Rnq1-based prions.
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 76 77 76 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 114 115 114 115 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 111 115 111 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 129 130 129 130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 126 130 126 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 154 163 154 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 200 201 200 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 389 396 389 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 431 440 431 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
(A) Reverse transmission barriers for passing the prion state from mini-[PIN+]s to full-length Rnq1. Data for [PIN+] to mini-[PIN+] transmission are from Figure 4A. Reverse transmission from mini-[PIN+]s was analyzed the same way; shown are averages for 8-13 independent experiments and SEM. (B) Requirement of a common QN region for the transmission of prion state between Rnq1 fragments in vivo. Experiments were performed as in Figure 1B. Donors of prion state are indicated on top, recipients are listed on the left. Shown is growth on SD-Ade after 21 days at 20degreesC. Lack of transmission was confirmed by NM::Yfp and Rnq1::Cfp aggregation tests (not shown).
###end p 63
###begin title 64
Transmission of the prion state between Rnq1 fragments.
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 33 43 33 43 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figures 1B</xref>
###xml 48 50 48 50 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">4A</xref>
###xml 500 501 500 501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 497 501 497 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 515 516 515 516 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 512 516 512 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Experiments were performed as in Figures 1B and 4A. (A) Each of the QN regions can transmit the prion state. In the schematic diagrams of Rnq1 deletion fragments QN1, QN2, QN3 and QN4 are in red, yellow, green and orange, respectively. Arrows indicate possibility of transmission between the indicated constructs. The only common QN region responsible for templaring is indicated near each arrow. (B-E) Barrier strength for the transmission of the prion state to Rnq1 fragments depends upon what [PIN+] or mini-[PIN+] is templating the conversion.
