###end p 65
###begin title 66
Discussion
###end title 66
###begin title 67
Multiple aggregation determinants of Rnq1
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 18 19 18 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 26 30 26 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URE3</italic>
###xml 37 38 37 38 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 34 38 34 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 197 206 197 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 371 378 371 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 383 391 383 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 600 607 600 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 747 756 747 756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 926 933 926 933 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 951 959 951 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1035 1044 1035 1044 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 1046 1055 1046 1055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
Together with [PSI+] and [URE3], [PIN+] belongs to the class of prions with QN-rich prion domains. The unique feature of Rnq1 is that it carries four QN regions separated by hydrophobic sequences (Figure 1A). Using a set of constructs retaining the entire N-terminal part of Rnq1 but bearing single and multiple deletions of QN regions in the C-terminus, we demonstrated in vivo and in vitro that prion domain of Rnq1 encompasses multiple prion determinants that can independently drive aggregation and transmit the prion state. Specifically, all four QN regions are able to transmit the prion state in vivo. Such transmission was demonstrated in experiments where the aggregated template and the recipient fragment had only one common QN region (Figure 7A). That transmission indeed occurred through the common QN sequences (that in our experimental system match exactly) was strongly indicated by two lines of evidence: (i) in vivo transmission and in vitro cross-seeding were completely blocked in the absence of common QN regions (Figure 2E, Figure 6B); (ii) the presence of one common QN region was generally sufficient for the transmission of the prion state to Rnq1 fragments that were otherwise known to maintain it.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 283 284 283 284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 280 284 280 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 299 300 299 300 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 296 300 296 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 408 409 405 406 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 405 409 402 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 424 425 421 422 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 421 425 418 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 782 783 747 748 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 779 783 744 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 786 795 751 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 819 820 784 785 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 816 820 781 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1079 1087 1044 1052 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1092 1100 1057 1065 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7</xref>
Our data also suggest that, in Rnq1-based prions, multiple aggregation determinants simultaneously take on conformations allowing them to transmit the prion state. Indeed, in order to template a QN region in a soluble Rnq1 fragment, the corresponding QN region in a pre-existing [PIN+] (or mini-[PIN+]) has to be in a transmissible conformation, e.g. engage in a beta-strand formation. And we found that [PIN+] and mini-[PIN+]s were each able to convert Rnq1 fragments carrying different sets of QN regions. For example, the ability of DeltaB1E4 to convert DeltaD3 and Delta2D indicates that in DeltaB1E4 both QN2 and QN3 were in a transmissible state, and conversion by DeltaB1C2 of DeltaD3 and DeltaE4 implies the transmissible state of both QN3 and QN4 in the DeltaB1C2 mini-[PIN+] (Figure 7A). For the original [PIN+], transmission to constructs carrying only QN2 or only QN4 proves simultaneous prionization of these QN regions, whereas aggregation of QN1 and QN3 is suggested by different strength of transmission barriers to constructs lacking or retaining these regions (Figure 3 and Figure 7).
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 127 128 127 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 156 163 156 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 173 174 173 174 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 170 174 170 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 552 560 552 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 926 930 926 930 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Alexandrov1">[75]</xref>
###xml 1086 1094 1086 1094 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1302 1303 1302 1303 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1299 1303 1299 1303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1420 1421 1420 1421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1417 1421 1417 1421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1541 1542 1533 1534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1538 1542 1530 1534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1718 1719 1698 1699 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1715 1719 1695 1699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1813 1822 1789 1798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 1854 1862 1826 1834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1941 1950 1913 1922 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g002">Figure 2E</xref>
###xml 2195 2196 2163 2164 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2192 2196 2160 2164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 2245 2246 2213 2214 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2242 2246 2210 2214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
Even though all four QN regions can transmit the prion state, the contribution of these determinants to the maintenance of [PIN+] may not be equal. Indeed, in vivo mini-[PIN+] formation was confirmed for all fragments encompassing either QN2 or QN4, but was not detected for fragments carrying only QN1 and/or QN3, suggesting that QN1 and QN3 cannot maintain the prion state in the absence of QN2 or QN4. We strongly favor this explanation for QN1, as QN1 construct retaining the upstream part of Rnq1 was shown to have very low aggregation propensity in vitro (only a short QN1 peptide free of N-terminal part of Rnq1 was able to form fibers). Furthermore, QN1's inability to maintain the prion state is not unexpected, as the QN1 region corresponds to roughly a half of other QN regions in length, lacks oligopeptide repeats and has no Y residues that were hypothesized to facilitate the fragmentation of amyloid aggregates [75]. It is not so expected for the QN3 region, which is more similar to QN2 and QN4 in length and organization, and could independently drive Rnq1 aggregation in vitro, even though QN3 fibers formed after a notably longer lag phase and had atypical seeding kinetics and reduced protease resistance. So we also contemplated the possibility that the failure to obtain mini-[PIN+]s maintained by QN3 alone (or in combination with QN1) was due to extremely strong transmission barrier between [PIN+] and DeltaB1C2E4 (or DeltaC2E4, respectively). So far we were unable to bypass this presumptive barrier using mini-[PIN+]s as donors of the prion conformation (MK and ID, unpublished observations). For example, no transmission to DeltaB1C2E4 or DeltaC2E4 was detected from the DeltaB1C2 mini-[PIN+], for which transmissible state of QN3 was indicated by the efficient conversion of DeltaE4 (Figure 7A). Our finding that DeltaB1C2E4 in vitro aggregation could not be seeded by fibers formed by QN3-containing fragments (Figure 2E) is consistent with either of the above explanations, as it could merely reflect the inability of the DeltaB1C2E4 fragment to form "mature" amyloid or indicate a conformational barrier. The remaining possibility that QN1 and QN3-based mini-[PIN+]s are unable to facilitate the induction of [PSI+], thus making our most sensitive test for the transmission of the prion state non-informative, is a subject of our further explorations.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 76 77 76 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 369 377 363 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 414 418 408 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Wickner3">[66]</xref>
###xml 458 465 452 459 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">153-405</sub>
###xml 1016 1019 1007 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Saupe1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1020 1024 1011 1015 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Ritter1">[76]</xref>
###xml 1066 1067 1057 1058 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1063 1067 1054 1058 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1497 1506 1460 1469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 1637 1641 1600 1604 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Krishnan1">[49]</xref>
###xml 1801 1810 1764 1773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
Our results provide a genetic framework for studies of the structure of [PIN+]. Out of several possible arrangements where multiple QN regions participate in beta-strand formation, our data are most consistent with the one where all QN regions form parallel in-register beta-sheets. This is in full agreement with a parallel in-register structure recently proposed for in vitro-made Rnq1 amyloid by Wickner et al. [66], who analyzed fibers formed by the Rnq1153-405 prion domain fragment by solid state NMR. Noteworthy, while Wickner et al. did not analyze the structure of different parts of the Rnq1 prion domain, their study utilized fibers with labeled Y residues, most of which are located in QN2, QN3 and QN4, indicating the applicability of the conclusion about parallel beta-sheet structure to these QN regions. Another possible structure postulating aggregated state of several QNs is where QN regions of the same molecule interact with each other, e.g. pair-wise in a pseudo-dimer [Het-s]-like arrangement [4],[76]. Such structure appears unlikely for [PIN+]: contrary to the expectation of such arrangements, we found no evidence that aggregation of any QN region in Rnq1-based prions depended on the presence of another QN region. For example, we detected transmission of the prion state relying on the QN4 aggregation from Delta2D, Delta3E or DeltaB1C2; transmission relying on QN3 from either DeltaB1C2 or DeltaB1E4; and transmission relying on QN2 from either Delta3E or DeltaB1E4 (Figure 7A). Finally, structures where duplicated oligopeptides within repeat-carrying QN regions engage in intramolecular self-interactions [49] are also not indicated by our data, since deleting one of the two oligopeptides in a repeat was not equivalent to complete elimination of the repeated region (Figure 5A), and such equivalency is expected if repeated oligopeptides interacted.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 188 189 188 189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 185 189 185 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 195 197 195 197 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sc</sup>
###xml 398 402 386 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Tessier1">[34]</xref>
###xml 403 407 391 395 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Krishnan1">[49]</xref>
###xml 408 412 396 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Toyama1">[50]</xref>
###xml 497 501 485 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Bradley2">[48]</xref>
###xml 526 534 514 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 534 538 522 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Glover1">[77]</xref>
###xml 539 543 527 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-King3">[78]</xref>
###xml 689 693 677 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Solforosi1">[79]</xref>
###xml 797 801 785 789 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Ostapchenko1">[80]</xref>
###xml 860 864 848 852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Vanik1">[46]</xref>
###xml 920 924 908 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Bertho1">[81]</xref>
###xml 931 935 919 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URE3</italic>
###xml 1106 1113 1094 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de novo</italic>
###xml 1130 1134 1118 1122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Maddelein1">[82]</xref>
Do other prions encompass multiple aggregation determinants that maintain a certain degree of independence? Such possibility is feasible for prions with complex prion domains, such as [PSI+], PrPSc and [Het-s]. Indeed, recent evidence indicates the presence of two distinct self-interacting regions within the Sup35 prion domain, one within the first 40 aa, and the other at approximately90-120 aa [34],[49],[50]. The second region appears to be expendable for the transmission of the prion state [48] and for fiber formation in vitro[77],[78], whereas expendability of the first region has never been tested directly. Similarly, four self-interacting regions have been identified for PrP [79]. The first of them, although not needed for prion replication, affects the structure of amyloid fibers [80], and the last, while being expendable for fiber formation [46], was hypothesized to be implicated in prion conversion [81]. For [URE3], the existence of a secondary prion-inducing region was considered upon the discovery of sequences in the non-prion domain part of Ure2, which facilitated/inhibited the de novo prion induction [82], but there is no evidence of multiple aggregation domains.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 305 309 305 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Resende1">[26]</xref>
###xml 437 438 437 438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 434 438 434 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 497 501 497 501 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Nakayashiki1">[24]</xref>
###xml 502 506 502 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Resende1">[26]</xref>
###xml 651 663 651 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s1">Introduction</xref>
###xml 767 768 767 768 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 764 768 764 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 482 487 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
On the other hand, prion domain of Rnq1 stands out as the most complex among known prion domains. The redundancy of its structure is the result of several duplication events, with most recent duplications that created oligopeptide repeats in three out of four QN regions still traceable at the DNA level ([26] and our unpublished data). Considering that so far no cellular function has been assigned to non-aggregated Rnq1, and that [PIN+] was detected in industrial and pathogenic yeast isolates [24],[26], and has been shown to interact with prions and aggregation-prone proteins affecting formation, stability and toxicity of various amyloids (see Introduction), functional performance of the Rnq1 protein may involve formation of oligomeric complexes, if not [PIN+] itself. In this case redundant aggregation-prone sub-domains are likely to improve ability of Rnq1 to self-interact and broaden the repertoire of possible heterologous interactions.
###end p 73
###begin title 74
Transmission barriers in the absence of amino acid mismatches in transmitting regions
###end title 74
###begin p 75
###xml 109 113 109 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Pattison1">[83]</xref>
###xml 350 358 350 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 363 370 363 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 502 506 502 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Chen1">[37]</xref>
###xml 507 511 507 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Vanik1">[46]</xref>
###xml 512 516 512 516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Chien1">[84]</xref>
###xml 517 521 517 521 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Prusiner2">[85]</xref>
###xml 904 916 904 916 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s1">Introduction</xref>
###xml 1137 1141 1137 1141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Tessier1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1142 1146 1142 1146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Solforosi1">[79]</xref>
###xml 1147 1151 1147 1151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Surewicz1">[86]</xref>
###xml 1152 1156 1152 1156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Langedijk1">[87]</xref>
###xml 94 99 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goats</span>
###xml 104 108 <span type="species:ncbi:10090|species:ncbi:10095">mice</span>
###xml 289 295 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 396 401 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Transmission barriers were discovered upon attempting to transmit scrapie infectious agent to goats and mice [83]. The presence and strength of transmission barriers determines the possibility and efficiency of prion transmission between non-identical proteins, e.g. the risk of infecting humans with prions originating in wild and domestic animals. In vitro and in vivo studies of mammalian and yeast prions relate these barriers to species-specific differences in primary sequences of prion proteins [37],[46],[84],[85]. A search for the explanation of how differences in primary structure, and specifically single aa substitutions, can control the tightness of the transmission barriers led to the model based on the recognition element concept. According to this concept, transmission of the prion state requires the interaction between clearly defined critical regions, or recognition elements (see Introduction). Consequently, the model for transmission barriers postulates that non-matching aa residues within these regions may impose the barrier by disrupting the productive interaction of the recipient protein and the template [34],[79],[86],[87]. Thus, the strength of such barriers depends on the degree of sequence dissimilarity within this short region, and on the conformation of the recognition element in the template (i.e. the prion strain), which determines whether, and to what extent, a particular aa mismatch will affect the barrier. An absolute barrier is expected if the interaction is impossible, e.g. in the absence of a common recognition element. In our experimental system transmission is driven by four QN regions. While we do not explore the effects on transmission of individual aa mismatches within the common QN regions, the lack of transmission between Rnq1 fragments with no common QN regions could exemplify the absolute barrier mentioned above.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 156 159 156 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Collinge1">[6]</xref>
###xml 160 164 160 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Bishop1">[88]</xref>
###xml 165 169 165 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Cancellotti1">[89]</xref>
###xml 1013 1014 1013 1014 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1010 1014 1010 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Yet, it would be an oversimplification to assume that all transmission barriers can be explained by primary structure dissimilarity in recognition elements [6],[88],[89]. Our study identifies and offers an explanation for transmission barriers not involving individual aa mismatches in recognition elements between the template and the recipient. We established that barriers exist for the transmission from full-length Rnq1 to Rnq1 fragments lacking any of the QN-rich aggregation determinants, and between all Rnq1 fragments encompassing non-identical sets of QN regions. At the same time, common QN regions, which drive the transmission across these non-absolute barriers, have fully matching sequences. Explaining these results in the framework of the abovementioned transmission barrier model is difficult, as it will involve postulating that deletion of any QN region changes the conformation of recognition elements in all other QN regions. However, our results are expected if overall conformation of [PIN+] and other Rnq1-based prions were a product of co-operative action of several aggregation domains. In this case a transmission barrier will form as a result of the inability of a recipient lacking some (or having extra) QN regions to take on exactly the same higher-order fold as the template. This distinct type of barrier will reflect a requirement for a conformational change at a higher level of amyloid structure despite conservation of identical primary structure and possibility of transmission within the recognition element(s) in common QN regions.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 477 478 477 478 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 474 478 474 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 952 953 952 953 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 949 953 949 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1037 1046 1037 1046 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 1370 1373 1370 1373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Collinge1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1374 1378 1374 1378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Vanik1">[46]</xref>
###xml 1379 1383 1379 1383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Tanaka2">[47]</xref>
###xml 1437 1438 1437 1438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1434 1438 1434 1438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
Upon further analysis of across-the-barrier transmission we gained additional support for the existence of transmission barriers determined by higher order conformational mismatches. (i) Since the recognition element is retained, such transmission barriers are likely to be non-absolute. Indeed, the presence of a common QN region was sufficient for the across-the-barrier transmission of the prion state to all constructs that were otherwise shown to be able to form mini-[PIN+]s. (ii) Also, while the interaction at the templating interface in the absence of aa mismatches may determine the same arrangement of the templating region in the newly forming prion, higher order conformation of this prion will be different. So prions forming by overcoming such transmission barriers are expected to have reverse barriers toward the proteins they were templated with. Indeed, reverse barriers were detected when transmitting the prion state from mini-[PIN+]s to full-length Rnq1; the strength of reverse barriers was not always reciprocal (Figure 5A). Importantly, inefficient reverse transmission is not predicted and was not observed for transmission barriers that are likely to be due to aa mismatches in recognition elements and where the transmission is presumed to occur through the selection of a recipient conformer compatible with the conformation of the template [6],[46],[47]. (iii) Recovery of both stable and unstable mini-[PIN+]s that indicates formation of prion strains during across-the-barrier transmission (MK and ID unpublished observations) is also expected when new prion folds are forming.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 399 403 399 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Resende1">[26]</xref>
###xml 494 495 494 495 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 491 495 491 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 758 762 758 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Tessier1">[34]</xref>
###xml 764 768 764 768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Krishnan1">[49]</xref>
###xml 769 773 769 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Chang1">[51]</xref>
###xml 844 845 844 845 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 841 845 841 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1037 1038 1037 1038 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1034 1038 1034 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1106 1107 1106 1107 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1103 1107 1103 1107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1134 1138 1134 1138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Shkundina1">[41]</xref>
###xml 1483 1487 1480 1484 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Gorfe1">[90]</xref>
###xml 238 243 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 248 253 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 505 510 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Some naturally occurring transmission barriers may be very similar to the ones described in our work, being based exclusively on higher-order conformations. For example, deletions and expansions of oligopeptide repeats are common both in yeast and human prion proteins. Rnq1 variants lacking oligopeptide repeats in QN3 and QN4 of Rnq1 were uncovered in a significant proportion of natural isolates [26]. Our data predict that these differences will impose barriers for the transmission of [PIN+] between yeast populations. The same study describes a Sup35 variant lacking two of the repeated oligopeptides. The Sup35 oligopeptide repeat region appears to be outside of recognition elements, but is involved in an ordered structure in the prion conformation [34], [49]-[51]. In this case previously demonstrated inefficient transmission of [PSI+] to Sup35 fragments with deletions in the oligopeptide repeat region can in part be due to transmission barriers. This possibility is consistent with a relatively high stability of "mini-[PSI+]" isolates originating from cultures, which were predominantly [psi-] after such transmissions [41]. Barriers determined by differences outside recognition elements may also play critical role in TSE epidemiology, specifically in limiting the spread of chronic wasting disease from cervides to other mammals. The 166-175 loop of PrP has been proposed to determine this transmission barrier, apparently without engaging in beta-strand formation [90]. In summary, our work reveals the existence of transmission barriers in the absence of aa mismatches in transmitting regions and introduces the concept of distinct types of transmission barriers for complex prion domains. Forthcoming information on recognition elements for various prions should help determine the nature of established barriers and further elucidate their role in prion transmission.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
Materials and Methods
###end title 79
###begin title 80
Plasmids
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 27 31 27 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 110 114 110 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 133 136 133 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CEN</italic>
###xml 150 154 150 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 163 167 163 167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 302 306 302 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 437 445 437 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CEN HIS3</italic>
###xml 514 518 514 518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Derkatch3">[52]</xref>
###xml 555 559 555 559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL1</italic>
###xml 573 581 573 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CEN URA3</italic>
###xml 635 639 635 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 647 650 647 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CFP</italic>
###xml 672 676 672 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CUP1</italic>
###xml 737 748 737 748 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s014">Protocol S1</xref>
###xml 753 762 753 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s010">Tables S1</xref>
###xml 764 766 764 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s011">S2</xref>
###xml 768 770 768 770 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s012">S3</xref>
###xml 60 65 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 351 356 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Plasmids for expression of RNQ1 and its deletion alleles in yeast were constructed on the backbone of pRS416 (URA3) or pRS415 (LEU2) CEN vectors; the RNQ1 ORF and RNQ1 fragments are controlled by the RNQ1 promoter and followed by the RNQ1 terminator sequence. To obtain bacterial expression constructs RNQ1 fragments were amplified from corresponding yeast plasmids and cloned into pJC45 to yield N-terminally 10xHIS-tagged proteins. In CEN HIS3-marked pGAL-SUP35NM::YFP, the previously used Sup35NM::Yfp reporter [52] was placed under the control of the GAL1 promoter. In CEN URA3-marked pCUP-RNQ::CFP, a fusion of complete wild type RNQ1 ORF to CFP is controlled by the CUP1 promoter. Plasmid construction and primers are described in Protocol S1 and Tables S1, S2, S3.
###end p 81

###xml 1111 1112 1099 1100 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1108 1112 1096 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1117 1118 1105 1106 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1114 1118 1102 1106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1166 1167 1154 1155 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1163 1167 1151 1155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1172 1173 1160 1161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1169 1173 1157 1161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1185 1189 1173 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1</italic>
###xml 1226 1227 1210 1211 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1223 1227 1207 1211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1232 1233 1216 1217 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1229 1233 1213 1217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1262 1266 1246 1250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
Unless otherwise mentioned, all strains are derivatives of 74-D694 (MATaade1-14 leu2-3,112 his3-Delta200 trp1-289 ura3-52; [91]). The [PIN+][psi-] derivative is 1Y1 [48]. The [pin-][psi-] derivative is 1G4 [53], obtained from 1Y1 by GuHCl treatment [92]. The rnq1-Delta 74-D694 [PIN+][psi-] strain was constructed by seamlessly disrupting the complete RNQ1 ORF using the integration-excision approach [93]. The pRS406-based URA3 disrupting plasmid, pID130, contained the RNQ1 promoter inserted as the EcoRI - BamHI fragment (primers #19 and #3; see Table S3) and the sequence downstream of the RNQ1 gene inserted as the SacII - SacI fragment (primers #31 and #32). During the disruption, the [PIN+] state was maintained by wild type RNQ1 expressed from the LEU2-marked maintainer (see Plasmids). To facilitate subsequent plasmid shuffles, the URA3-marked maintainer was substituted for the LEU2-marked maintainer after disruption. To monitor the presence of [PIN+], the tightly regulated pGAL-SUP35NM::YFP CEN HIS3 plasmid was introduced prior to the disruption and was maintained in the rnq1-Delta 74-D694 [PIN+][psi-] strain during subsequent experiments. The [pin-][psi-]version of rnq1-Delta 74-D694 was obtained from [PIN+][psi-]by transiently removing the RNQ1 maintainer.
###end p 83

###xml 8 9 8 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 14 15 14 15 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 11 15 11 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 25 28 25 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 28 33 28 29 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</bold>
###xml 33 77 29 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ade1-14 leu2-3,112 lys9-A21 trp1-289 ura3-52</italic>

The [pin-][psi-] 64-D697 MATalphaade1-14 leu2-3,112 lys9-A21 trp1-289 ura3-52[53] was used in crosses to introduce pCUP-RNQ-CFP for the Rnq1::Cfp aggregation test.

###begin title 85
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Yeast methods and cultivation procedures
###end title 85
###begin p 86
###xml 58 62 58 62 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Rose1">[94]</xref>
###xml 63 67 63 67 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Sherman1">[95]</xref>
###xml 365 368 353 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL</italic>
###xml 465 468 453 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CUP</italic>
###xml 540 541 524 525 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 625 629 609 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 646 650 630 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Boeke1">[96]</xref>
###xml 9 14 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 100 105 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Standard yeast media and cultivation procedures were used [94],[95]. Unless specifically mentioned, yeast were grown at 30degreesC on solid synthetic glucose media (SD) selective for plasmid maintenance. Cultures for transformation and protein isolation were grown in liquid organic complete YPD medium at 30degreesC with constant orbital agitation at 200 rpm. The GAL promoter was induced on synthetic media with 2% galactose as a single carbon source (SGal). The CUP promoter was induced on synthetic media supplemented with 20microM CuSO4. Media supplemented with 5-fluoroorotic acid was used for selective elimination of URA3-marked plasmids [96].
###end p 86

###xml 977 987 977 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 1060 1061 1056 1057 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1057 1061 1053 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1093 1105 1089 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SUP35NM::YFP</italic>
###xml 575 580 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 766 771 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The [PSI+] induction assay relies on the requirement of [PIN+] for the de novo formation of [PSI+] and requires that the strain carry a [PSI+]-inducing construct and a reporter for the detection of [PSI+] ([53]; reviewed in [69]). [PSI+]-inducing constructs expressing the prion domain of the [PSI+]-forming protein, Sup35, allow for the increase of [PIN+]-dependent appearance of [PSI+] to readily detectable levels. In our experiments, the strain carried the SUP35NM::YFP fusion under the control of a tightly regulated GAL1 promoter. The promoter remained repressed while yeast were growing on glucose media prior to shuffling out the wild type RNQ1 maintainer. After elimination of full-length RNQ1, expression of pGAL-SUP35NM::YFP was turned on by transferring yeast to galactose medium. To allow for the detection of [PSI+], the strain carried the ade1-14 reporter, a premature stop codon in the chromosomal ADE1 gene. The ade1-14 mutation made the original [PIN+][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 strain unable to grow on media lacking adenine. However, in [PSI+] cells that appeared following SUP35NM::YFP overexpression, translation termination was compromised due to Sup35 aggregation, which resulted in nonsense suppression, i.e. occasional readthrough of the stop codon detectable as slow growth on -Ade.
###end p 88
###begin p 89
###xml 10 14 10 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 59 60 59 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 56 60 56 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 65 66 65 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 62 66 62 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 68 78 68 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1-&#916;</italic>
###xml 98 102 94 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 110 114 106 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 132 135 128 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS</italic>
###xml 165 166 161 162 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 162 166 158 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 303 304 299 300 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 378 379 374 375 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 375 379 371 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 438 439 434 435 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 435 439 431 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 828 829 812 813 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 872 873 856 857 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 869 873 853 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 893 897 877 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Tuite1">[92]</xref>
###xml 952 957 936 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 957 961 941 945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Derkatch1">[18]</xref>
###xml 405 410 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 750 755 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Indicated LEU2-marked constructs were transformed into [psi-][PIN+] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 carrying a URA3-marked RNQ1 maintainer and a HIS-marked pGAL-SUP35NM::YFP [PSI+]-inducer. Transformants were selected on SD-Leu,Ura,His and then passed twice on SD-Leu,His to allow for the loss of the maintainer. Ura- cells were selected on FOA and transferred to SGal-Leu,His to induce [PSI+]. From galactose medium, yeast were replica plated to [PSI+] scoring media, SD-Ade and SEt-Ade (synthetic media containing, respectively, 2% glucose or 2% ethanol as a single carbon source) and to SD-Leu,His (growth control). SD-Ade and SEt-Ade plates were incubated at 20degreesC and 30degreesC and scored several times between days 5 and 25. In the control experiment yeast were grown on non-inducing SD-Leu,His prior to suppression analysis. Ade+ colonies were further confirmed to be [PSI+] by the GuHCl test [92], which was performed exactly as described in Derkatch et al[18] on media supplemented with 5 mM guanidine hydrochloride (GuHCl).
###end p 89
###begin p 90
###xml 18 19 18 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 136 137 136 137 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 133 137 133 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 215 216 215 216 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 212 216 212 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 324 328 324 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Patino1">[70]</xref>
###xml 329 333 329 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Zhou1">[71]</xref>
Additionally, [PSI+] induction was monitored by fluorescent microscopy of cultures grown on galactose medium using the Sup35NM::Yfp [PSI+]-inducer as a reporter: incorporation of Sup35NM::Yfp into newly forming [PSI+] aggregates allowed their visualization by fluorescent microscopy as characteristic ring-shaped structures [70],[71].
###end p 90
###begin title 91
Rnq1::Cfp aggregation assay
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 23 27 23 27 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Liebman1">[69]</xref>
###xml 162 166 162 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Patino1">[70]</xref>
###xml 218 222 218 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1</italic>
###xml 255 259 251 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 267 271 263 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
###xml 305 306 301 302 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 302 306 298 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pin<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 336 340 332 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 481 482 473 474 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 558 559 550 551 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 555 559 547 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
The assay (reviewed in [69]) relies on the ability of fusions of prion proteins with fluorescent reporters to join prion aggregates and allow their visualization [70]. The Rnq1::Cfp reporter was introduced by crossing rnq1-Delta 74-D694 cultures carrying LEU2-marked RNQ1 deletion constructs with the [pin-] 64-D697 strain carrying the URA3-marked pCUP-RNQ1::CFP plasmid. Diploids were selected on SD-Ura,Leu. The reporter was induced by supplementing SD-Ura,Leu with 20microM CuSO4. Presence of cells with bright fluorescent foci was indicative of mini-[PIN+]s.
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 85 92 85 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de novo</italic>
###xml 111 112 111 112 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 108 112 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 121 122 121 122 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 118 122 118 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psi<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 168 172 168 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Derkatch2">[19]</xref>
###xml 193 200 193 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">de novo</italic>
###xml 218 219 218 219 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 242 246 242 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnq1</italic>
###xml 294 298 290 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ1</italic>
Note: moderate short-term (2-3 days) overexpression of Rnq1::Cfp does not induce the de novo appearance of [PIN+] in [psi-] strains, which were used in our experiments [19]. To confirm lack of de novo induction of [PIN+] in the diploids, the rnq1-Delta 74-D694 carrying empty vector instead of RNQ1 deletion constructs was included in all crosses.
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Rnq1 sedimentation assays
###end title 94
###begin p 95
###xml 49 53 49 53 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Liebman1">[69]</xref>
###xml 589 599 575 585 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s002">Figure S2D</xref>
###xml 703 707 689 693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-Lopez1">[97]</xref>
###xml 709 718 695 704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 720 732 706 718 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g004">Figure 4C&#8211;4E</xref>
###xml 734 743 720 729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 749 759 735 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s002">Figure S2B</xref>
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Yeast cell lysates were prepared as described in [69] except that pre-clearing at 10,000xg was omitted. 60 microg of total protein were centrifuged at 280,000xg for 30 min at 4degreesC (Beckman Optima TLX centrifuge, TLA 120.2 rotor). After removing the supernatant (S), the pellet fraction (P) was resuspended in the protein extraction buffer. The S and P fractions and 60 microg of total lysate (T) were separated by SDS-PAGE. Rnq1 was detected by a Western blot with polyclonal antibodies raised against full-length Rnq1 (Type 2, a generous gift from S. Lindquist, Whitehead Institute; Figure S2D) or the N-terminal Rnq1 fragment (Rnq1A, kindly provided by E. Craig, University of Wisconsin-Madison; [97]; Figure 3C, Figure 4C-4E, Figure S1, and Figure S2B).
###end p 95
###begin title 96
Recombinant protein purification
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 122 130 122 130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s011">Table S2</xref>
###xml 268 271 258 261 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 648 649 614 615 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 651 652 617 618 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 0 21 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">Escherichia coli BL21</span>
Escherichia coli BL21-AI One Shot cells (Invitrogen) transformed with pJC45-based expression constructs (see Plasmids and Table S2) were cultured in LB medium supplemented with 100 microg/ml ampicillin at 37degreesC. Protein expression was induced at mid-log phase (OD600approximately0.4) by 1mM IPTG and 0.2% L-arabinose for 1.5 h. Cells were harvested by centrifugation (4degreesC, 1600xg) and either processed immediately or frozen at -80degreesC. Due to limited solubility of Rnq1 in aqueous solutions, purification was carried out under denaturing conditions at room temperature. Cells were lysed by gentle agitation in lysis buffer (100mM NaH2PO4 pH 7.4, 350mM NaCl, 8M urea) for 1h. Cell debris was removed by centrifugation at 20,000xg for 10 min. Supernatant was incubated for 2 h with Ni-NTA Sepharose (Qiagen) equilibrated with lysis buffer. The slurry was transferred to the column and washed extensively with lysis buffer. Rnq1 was eluted with lysis buffer containing 250mM imidazole. Protein enriched fractions were determined by UV absorption at 280nm and concentrated on Centricons (Millipore). Protein concentration was determined by the BCA assay (Pierce). Purity of recombinant proteins was estimated by SDS-PAGE as >95%.
###end p 97
###begin title 98
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
In vitro fiber formation
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 96 97 92 93 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 99 100 95 96 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 201 205 193 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000824-LeVine1">[98]</xref>
###xml 264 266 251 253 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ex</sub>
###xml 264 266 251 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>ex</sub></italic>
###xml 281 283 263 265 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">em</sub>
###xml 281 283 263 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>em</sub></italic>
The 200 microl reactions were set up in assembly buffer (1M urea, final concentration; 100mM NaH2PO4 pH 7.4; 300mM NaCl) in the presence 5 microM ThT. Fiber formation was monitored by ThT fluorescence [98] in a Molecular Devices SpectraMax M-5 plate reader (lambdaex 450 nm; lambdaem 483 nm; 24degreesC). Readings were taken every 15 min, samples were shaken for 5 sec prior to each reading. For each protein, experiments were performed in duplicate and repeated at least 3 times. To obtain fibers for seeded reactions, suspensions of polymerized Rnq1 fragments were collected from the wells and precipitated with 5 volumes of Met-OH. Pellets were washed 3 times with 70% Et-OH to remove urea, and then dried with anhydrous acetone. Seed powder was stored at 4degreesC and dissolved in the assembly buffer right before adding to the samples. Papain digestions were performed at 25degreesC for 30 min. Papain (Sigma) was added directly to ThT reactions (enzyme:substrate ratio 1:50).
###end p 99
###begin title 100
Fluorescence microscopy
###end title 100
###begin p 101
Cells were observed using an Axioplan2 Zeiss microscope. Images of representative fields were captured with a Zeiss Axiocam digital camera and processed with Improvision OpenLab software. Fluorescence and differential interference contrast images (DIC) are shown for each field.
###end p 101
###begin title 102
Transmission electron microscopy (TEM)
###end title 102
###begin p 103
TEM was performed at the NYU School of Medicine Image Core Facility. Fiber suspensions in the assembly buffer were diluted 2.5-fold in water and 4 microl were applied onto the carbon-coated 400 mesh Cu/Rh grids (Ted Pella Inc.). The grid was washed 3 times with water to get rid of urea, and negatively stained with 1% uranyl acetate (twice briefly and then for 5 min at 25degreesC). Images were obtained using Philips CM12 transmission electron microscope supplied with a Gatan 1kx1k digital camera and processed using Gatan Digital Micrograph software.
###end p 103

###xml 1235 1244 1231 1240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s008">Figure S8</xref>
###xml 1250 1259 1246 1255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000824.s009">Figure S9</xref>
###xml 1369 1370 1365 1366 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1366 1370 1362 1366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1486 1487 1482 1483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1483 1487 1479 1483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNQ<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 32 37 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 468 473 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
###xml 1382 1387 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Expression of Rnq1 fragments in yeast. Western blot analysis of the lysates of [PIN+][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 cells co-expressing Rnq1 and the indicated deletion constructs. Both full-length RNQ1 and its fragments are controlled by the native RNQ1 promoter (see Plasmids in Materials and Methods, and Protocol S1 for plasmid construction). Transformants were maintained on the medium selective for both plasmids, but cultures for protein isolation were grown in YPD. Yeast cell lysates were prepared as described in Liebman et al. [2006] except that pre-clearing at 10,000xg was omitted. Rnq1 was detected with polyclonal antibodies raised against the N-terminal part of the protein ([Lopez et al., 2003]; kindly provided by E. Craig, University of Wisconsin-Madison). Panels show same lanes in the top and bottom parts of the Western blot of the same culture. All Rnq1 fragments ran in accordance with their expected size. At least 2 independent transformants were analyzed for each construct and experiments were repeated 2-5 times. The groups are: deletions of one (A), two (B) and three (C) QN regions with preceding hydrophobic patches used throughout the manuscript; and (D) other constructs used mostly in Figure 5, Figure S2, Figure S8, and Figure S9. (Liebman SW, Bagriantsev SN, Derkatch IL (2006) Biochemical and genetic methods for characterization of [PIN+] prions in yeast. Methods 39: 23-34.) (Lopez N, Aron R, Craig EA (2003) The role of Sis1 on the maintenance of [RNQ+] prion. Mol Biol Cell 14: 1172-1181.)

###xml 809 813 801 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 861 870 853 862 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 895 896 887 888 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 892 896 884 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1075 1076 1063 1064 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1072 1076 1060 1064 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1123 1124 1111 1112 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1120 1124 1108 1112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1311 1313 1291 1293 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">10</sub>
###xml 1418 1419 1394 1395 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1475 1476 1451 1452 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1472 1476 1448 1452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1524 1533 1500 1509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000824-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 1781 1782 1753 1754 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1778 1782 1750 1754 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 2110 2114 2082 2086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URE3</italic>
###xml 1981 1986 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The QN-rich C-terminus is an essential part of the prion domain of Rnq1. N-terminal Rnq1 fragments were previously shown to be unable to join [PIN+] or to transmit the prion state [Vitrenko et al., 2007]. However, in those studies Rnq1 fragments were Gfp-tagged, and large tags sometimes interfere with prion properties [Dagkesamanskaia et al., 1997; Edskes et al., 1999]. We confirm that the QN-rich C-terminus is indispensable for mini-[PIN+]s in our experimental setup, and demonstrate that QG10 is not required for mini-[PIN+] establishment. (A,B) DeltaB1C2D3E4, a Rnq1 fragment lacking all QN regions but retaining QG10, does not aggregate in [PIN+] cells and does not carry on the Pin+ phenotype. (A) Cultures expressing DeltaB1C2D3E4 become Pin- upon the loss of full-length Rnq1. Plasmid shuffle and [PSI+] induction test were performed as described in Figure 1B legend. The lack of [PSI+] formation was confirmed by fluorescent microscopy using the Sup35NM::Yfp reporter (not shown). (B) There is no evidence of DeltaB1C2D3E4 aggregation even in the presence of [PIN+]. Sedimentation analysis of the lysate of [PIN+] cells co-expressing Rnq1 and DeltaB1C2D3E4; panels show same lanes in the top and bottom parts of the Western blot of the same culture. Similar data for Delta1C2D3E4 not shown. (C,D) QG10 is not essential for maintaining the prion state of Rnq1: DeltaQG is aggregated, and cultures remain Pin+ after elimination of Rnq1. (C) Plasmid shuffle and [PSI+] induction test were performed as described in Figure 1B legend. (D) Sedimentation analysis of cell lysates from cultures expressing indicated fragments after elimination of full-length Rnq1. Similar data for DeltaAQG not shown. (Vitrenko YA, Pavon ME, Stone SI, Liebman SW (2007) Propagation of the [PIN+] prion by fragments of Rnq1 fused to GFP. Curr Genet 51: 309-319.) (Dagkesamanskaia AR, Kushnirov VV, Paushkin SV, Ter-Avanesyan MD (1997) Fusion of glutathione S-transferase with the N-terminus of yeast Sup35 protein inhibits its prion-like properties. Genetika (Rus) 33: 610-615.) (Edskes HK, Gray VT, Wickner RB (1999) The [URE3] prion is an aggregated form of Ure2p that can be cured by overexpression of Ure2p fragments. Proc Natl Acad Sci USA 96: 1498-1503.)
###end p 108

###begin p 111
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 170 178 170 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1107 1128 1053 1074 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 1282 1303 1228 1249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
In vitro analysis of aggregation of Rnq1 protein fragments and QN1 peptide. (A) Cross-seeding between Rnq1 protein fragments lacking two or three QN regions. Kinetics of in vitro aggregation was monitored by ThT fluorescence. The soluble protein is indicated above the graphs, and seeds are listed to the right in brackets. "No seed" indicates unseeded polymerization. Proteins used: QN2 (DeltaB1D3E4), QN3 (DeltaB1C2E4), QN4 (DeltaB1C2D3), QN1,2 (DeltaD3E4), QN3,4 (DeltaB1C2). Concentrations of soluble proteins were in the 60-80 microM range. (B) Transmission electron micrographs of negatively stained QN1 peptide fibers. The 12 aa long QN1 peptide (NSNNNNQQGQNQ; GenScript; 98.8% purity) was pre-treated with 1,1,1,3,3,3,-hexafluoro-2-isopropanol (Sigma) for 24 h at room temperature and lyophilized. The powder was re-suspended in water to a final concentration of 250 microg/ml. The 200 microl reactions were set up in the presence of 5 microM ThT. Samples incubated at 37degreesC for approximately80 h were shaken for 5 sec every 10 min. Monitoring the aggregation kinetics by ThT fluorescence (see Materials and Methods) revealed a sigmoidal curve with a very short lag phase (not shown). TEM was performed at the NYU School of Medicine Image Core Facility as described in Materials and Methods. Long and very thin (<10 nm in diameter) fibers were frequently laterally associated and had either straight or twisted appearance.

###xml 266 269 262 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI</italic>
###xml 269 270 265 266 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 349 352 345 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI</italic>
###xml 352 353 348 349 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 609 612 605 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 612 613 608 609 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 703 706 699 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI</italic>
###xml 706 707 702 703 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 820 823 816 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI</italic>
###xml 823 824 819 820 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 948 951 944 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PIN</italic>
###xml 951 952 947 948 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1219 1220 1199 1200 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1216 1220 1196 1200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1501 1502 1457 1458 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1498 1502 1454 1458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 1698 1699 1654 1655 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1695 1699 1651 1655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PSI<sup>+</sup></italic>
Reduction of the de novo formation of [PSI+] after substitution of deletion constructs for full-length RNQ1. Plasmid shuffle was performed in the [PIN+][psi-] rnq1-Delta 74-D694 strain carrying the pGAL-SUP35NM::YFP [PSI+] inducer as described in Figure 1B legend. [PSI+] was induced by growth on SGal-Leu,His plates for 3 days. Relative levels of [PSI+] induction were calculated by determining the percentage of cells with Sup35NM-Yfp fluorescent aggregates in cultures expressing indicated constructs, and then normalizing it to the percentage of aggregate-containing cells in cultures carrying wild-type [PIN+] only. Each data point represents an independent experiment, in which the percentage of [PSI+] cells determined for three transformants expressing the deletion construct is normalized to the percentage of [PSI+] cells in three transformants expressing wild-type Rnq1 (a total of 500-1,000 cells were analyzed in each case; wild-type [PIN+] cultures carried 30-40% aggregate containing cells). Data for constructs DeltaC2 and Delta2D, and DeltaD3 and Delta3E were similar and are grouped. Among the constructs lacking only one of the four QN regions, elimination of QN4 had the biggest effect reducing [PSI+] induction approximately5-fold, whereas deleting QN2 or QN3 reduced it approximately2-fold. The effect of double deletions varied depending upon what QN regions were eliminated. Eliminating QN3 in conjunction with a lack of either QN2 or QN4 led to an almost 100-fold drop in [PSI+] induction, whereas deletion of QN1 only mildly increased the effect of eliminating QN3 and QN4 and, surprisingly, had a rescuing effect when deleted together with QN2. Finally, the level of [PSI+] induction was the lowest in cultures expressing the Rnq1 fragments with only one QN region.
